<!DOCTYPE html> at the top of a valid HTML5 document

Omitting the DOCTYPE results in unexpected rendering behavior across browsers ^WAflhB6M

Placing DOCTYPE after <html> or whitespace

Using lowercase or malformed variants like <!doctype html> (technically allowed, but discouraged in formal documentation)

Using obsolete DOCTYPEs like HTML 4.01 or XHTML in HTML5 documents ^pcS1dyBd

DOCTYPE in HTML5 vs. HTML 4.01: HTML5 uses a simplified syntax (<!DOCTYPE html>) with no URL to a DTD.

DOCTYPE vs. meta charset tag: DOCTYPE affects parsing mode; meta tags affect encoding. ^T4VqPzGL

The DOCTYPE declaration in HTML (<!DOCTYPE html>) is a required preamble at the very top of an HTML document that instructs the browser to render the page in standards mode. Specifically, <!DOCTYPE html> is the declaration used for HTML5 and signals to the browser to apply the HTML5 specification rules without triggering backward-compatibility modes (quirks mode or almost standards mode). It is case-insensitive but must appear as the first non-whitespace content in the document to be valid. Unlike earlier HTML versions, HTML5's DOCTYPE does not reference a DTD (Document Type Definition); it is a simplified declaration that preserves legacy compatibility while enforcing consistent parsing behavior. ^rTW7jeY7
